        </p><ol id="references" class="useLabel"><li id="ref1"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">1</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit1" data-doi="10.1016/0167-2738(94)90411-1"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ozawa, K.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Lithium-Ion Rechargeable Batteries with LiCoO<sub>2</sub> and Carbon Electrodes: The LiCoO<sub>2</sub>/C System</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Solid State Ionics</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1994</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">69</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">212</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">221</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/0167-2738(94)90411-1</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D69%26publication_year%3D1994%26pages%3D212-221%26journal%3DSolid%2BState%2BIonics%26author%3DK.%2BOzawa%26title%3DLithium-Ion%2BRechargeable%2BBatteries%2Bwith%2BLiCoO2%2Band%2BCarbon%2BElectrodes%253A%2BThe%2BLiCoO2%252FC%2BSystem%26doi%3D10.1016%252F0167-2738%252894%252990411-1&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b05326&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2F0167-2738%2894%2990411-1&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lithium-ion rechargeable batteries with LiCoO2 and carbon electrodes: the LiCoO2/C system</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ozawa, Kazunori</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Solid State Ionics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1994</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">69</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3-4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">212-21</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SSIOD3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0167-2738</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Li-ion rechargeable battery with LiCoO2 cathode and non-graphitizable C anode has high energy d.  By using LiPF6 electrolyte dissolved in propylene carbonate/diethyl carbonate soln., excellent cycle performance was obtained even at a moderately high temp., because (1) LiCoO2 remained stable, and (2) non-graphitizable C exhibited a good cyclability with respect to Li-doping/undoping capability.  Although a thin film is formed on the C surface during charge and discharge cycling, the discharge capacity degrdn. is only 10-20% after 500 cycles.  Furthermore, even if the cell is overcharged, safety can be attained by (1) providing an anti-overcharging safety device which operates when Li2CO3 in the cathode is decompd. and (2) using a polyolefin separator which shuts down at a high temp. due to overcharge current.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGolNFbZJp4t1rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgS4QK3vgJ3Sw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK2cXlvVenurY%253D&amp;md5=9410cf64e0551589d7385a92408e1585</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1038/35104644"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tarascon, J.-M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Armand, M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Issues and Challenges Facing Rechargeable Lithium Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nature</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2001</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">414</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">359</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">367</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrode materials for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries: potential alternatives to current lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Sung-Wook; Seo, Dong-Hwa; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium (Li)-ion batteries (LIB) have governed the current worldwide rechargeable battery market due to their outstanding energy and power capability.  In particular, the LIB's role in enabling elec. vehicles (EVs) has been highlighted to replace the current oil-driven vehicles in order to reduce the usage of oil resources and generation of CO2 gases.  Unlike Li, sodium is one of the more abundant elements on Earth and exhibits similar chem. properties to Li, indicating that Na chem. could be applied to a similar battery system.  In the 1970s-80s, both Na-ion and Li-ion electrodes were investigated, but the higher energy d. of Li-ion cells made them more applicable to small, portable electronic devices, and research efforts for rechargeable batteries have been mainly concd. on LIB since then.  Recently, research interest in Na-ion batteries (NIB) has been resurrected, driven by new applications with requirements different from those in portable electronics, and to address the concern on Li abundance.  In this article, both neg. and pos. electrode materials in NIB are briefly reviewed.  While the voltage is generally lower and the vol. change upon Na removal or insertion is larger for Na-intercalation electrodes, compared to their Li equiv., the power capability can vary depending on the crystal structures.  It is concluded that cost-effective NIB can partially replace LIB, but requires further investigation and improvement.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGonnrfiSUpaRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liUsQ_kbbr4AA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhtVOrtLjF&amp;md5=485b20393bb8876b2f69ca708aeba606</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1126/science.1212741"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dunn, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kamath, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tarascon, J.-M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrical Energy Storage for the Grid: A Battery of Choices</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Science</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">334</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">928</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">935</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

The increasing interest in energy storage for the grid can be attributed to multiple factors, including the capital costs of managing peak demands, the investments needed for grid reliability, and the integration of renewable energy sources.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Investigating the Energy Storage Mechanism of SnS2-rGO Composite Anode for Advanced Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Chuze; Xu, Jing; Alvarado, Judith; Qu, Baihua; Somerville, James; Lee, Jim Yang; Meng, Ying Shirley</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin sulfide-reduced graphene oxide (SnS2-rGO) composite material is investigated as an advanced anode material for Na-ion batteries.  It can deliver a reversible capacity of 630 mAh g-1 with negligible capacity loss and exhibits superb rate performance.  Here, the energy storage mechanism of this SnS2-rGO anode and the crit. mechanistic role of rGO will be revealed in detail.  A synergistic mechanism involving conversion and alloying reactions is proposed based on our synchrotron X-ray diffraction (SXRD) and in situ X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS) results.  Contrary to what has been proposed in the literature, we detd. that Na2S2 forms instead of Na2S at the fully discharge state.  The as-formed Na2S2 works as a matrix to relieve the strain from the huge vol. expansion of the Na-Sn alloy reaction, shown in the high resoln. transmission electron microscope (HRTEM).  In addn., the Raman spectra results suggest that the rGO not only assists the material to have better electrochem. performance by preventing particle agglomeration of the active material but also coordinates with Na-ions through electrostatic interaction during the first cycle.  The unique reaction mechanism in SnS2-rGO offers a well-balanced approach for sodium storage to deliver high capacity, long-cycle life, and superior rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoQ0HQeDv131bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9huhsEhqkJw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXht1Sgs7vN&amp;md5=12f7ae16a53d72721aecf9a2bd718688</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1039/C4EE03192J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, M.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A comprehensive review of sodium layered oxides: powerful cathodes for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Man Huon; Gonzalo, Elena; Singh, Gurpreet; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The room temp. Na-ion secondary battery has been under focus lately due to its feasibility to compete against the already well-established Li-ion secondary battery.  Although there are many obstacles to overcome before the Na-ion battery becomes com. available, recent research discoveries corroborate that some of the cathode materials for the Na-ion battery have indeed indisputable advantages over its Li-ion counterparts.  In this publication, a comprehensive review of layered oxides (NaTMO2, TM = Ti, V, Cr, Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, and a mixt. of 2 or 3 elements) as a viable Na-ion battery cathode is presented.  Single TM systems are well characterized not only for their electrochem. performance but also for their structural transitions during the cycle.  Binary TM systems are investigated in order to address issues regarding low reversible capacity, capacity retention, operating voltage, and structural stability.  As a consequence, some materials already have reached an energy d. of 520 mW h g-1, which is comparable to that of LiFePO4.  Furthermore, some ternary TM systems retained more than 72% of their capacity along with over 99.7% Coulombic efficiency for 275 cycles.  The goal of this review is to present the development of Na layered oxide materials in the past as well as the state of the art today in order to emphasize the compatibility and durability of layered oxides as powerful candidates for Na-ion battery cathode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpwo96Ash7WNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9huhsEhqkJw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVCrsLjE&amp;md5=d938be66a2a0948e3d2f589b803dbf76</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1016/j.elecom.2015.07.023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Meng, Y.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent Advances and Prospects of Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiang, Xingde; Zhang, Kai; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">36</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5343-5364</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Na-ion batteries (SIBs) receive significant attention for electrochem. energy storage and conversion owing to their wide availability and the low cost of Na resources.  However, SIBs face challenges of low specific energy, short cycling life, and insufficient specific power, owing to the heavy mass and large radius of Na+ ions.  As an important component of SIBs, cathode materials have a significant effect on the SIB electrochem. performance.  The most recent advances and prospects of inorg. and org. cathode materials are summarized here.  Among current cathode materials, layered transition-metal oxides achieve high specific energies around 600 mW h g-1 owing to their high specific capacities of 180-220 mA h g-1 and their moderate operating potentials of 2.7-3.2 V (vs. Na+/Na).  Porous Na3V2(PO4)3/C nanomaterials exhibit excellent cycling performance with almost 100% retention over 1000 cycles owing to their robust structural framework.  Recent emerging cathode materials, such as amorphous NaFePO4 and pteridine derivs. show interesting electrochem. properties and attractive prospects for application in SIBs.  Future work should focus on strategies to enhance the overall performance of cathode materials in terms of specific energy, cycling life, and rate capability with cationic doping, anionic substitution, morphol. fabrication, and electrolyte matching.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRG1Bub04s8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhXKTCVNAz6bw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlCjur7N&amp;md5=6d0a96f9e9421c02a9f3b48744267752</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1142/S1793604713300016"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, D. All the original Na can be extd. from P2-Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 and it can be reversibly inserted again.  When x &gt; 1/3 in Nax[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2, the compd. remains in the P2 structure.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered P2-Nax[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 (0 &lt; x &lt; 2/3) was studied as a cathode material for Na-ion batteries.  A combination of 1st principles computation, electrochem. and synchrotron characterizations is conducted to elucidate the working mechanism for the improved electrochem. properties.  The reversible phase transformation from P2 to O2 is obsd.  New configurations of Na-ions and vacancy are found at x = 1/3 and 1/2, which correspond to the intermediate phases upon the electrochem. cycling process.  The mobility of Na-ions is studied using the galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT) and the Na diffusion barriers are calcd. by the Nudged Elastic Band (NEB) method.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Direct evidence for high Na+ mobility and high voltage structural processes in P2-Nax[LiyNizMn1-y-z]O2 (x, y, z ≤ 1) cathodes from solid-state NMR and DFT calculations</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Clement, R. J.; Xu, J.; Middlemiss, D. S.; Alvarado, J.; Ma, C.; Meng, Y. S.; Grey, C. P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4129-4143</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Structural processes occurring upon electrochem. cycling in P2-Nax[LiyNizMn1-y-z]O2 (x, y, z ≤ 1) cathode materials are investigated using 23Na and 7Li solid-state NMR (ssNMR).  The interpretation of the complex paramagnetic NMR data obtained for various electrochem.-cycled NaxNi1/3Mn2/3O2 and NaxLi0.12Ni0.22Mn0.66O2 samples is assisted by state-of-the-art hybrid Hartree-Fock/d. functional theory calcns.  Two Na crystallog. environments are present in P2-Nax[LiyNizMn1-y-z]O2 compds., yet a single 23Na NMR signal is obsd. with a shift in-between those computed for edge- and face-centered prismatic sites, indicating that Na-ion motion between sites in the P2 layers results in an av. signal.  This is the first time that exptl. and theor. evidence are provided for fast Na-ion motion (on the timescale of the NMR expts.) in the interlayer space in P2-type NaxTMO2 materials.  A full assignment of the 7Li NMR data confirms that Li substitution delays the P2 to O2 phase transformation taking place in NaxNi1/3Mn2/3O2 over the range 1/3 ≥ xNa ≥ 0. 23Na ssNMR data demonstrate that NaxNi1/3Mn2/3O2 samples charged to ≥3.7 V are extremely moisture sensitive once they are removed from the cell, water mols. being readily intercalated within the P2 layers leading to an addnl. Na signal between 400 and 250 ppm.  By contrast, the lithiated material NaxLi0.12Ni0.22Mn0.66O2 shows no sign of hydration until it is charged to ≥4.4 V.  Since both TMO2 layer glides and water intercalation become increasingly favorable as more vacancies are present in the Na layers, the higher stability of the Li-doped P2 phase at high voltage can be accounted for by its higher Na content at all stages of cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrbqKD91fdxurVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhXKTCVNAz6bw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXht1OksLo%253D&amp;md5=52bb856d8fe7b094a68d01cd03da72df</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1149/2.0201514jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Clément, R.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Review-Manganese-Based P2-Type Transition Metal Oxides as Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode Materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Clement, Raphaele J.; Bruce, Peter G.; Grey, Clare P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">162</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">A2589-A2604</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JESOAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium transition metal oxides (NaMO2) with a P2 structure exhibit good Na+ ion cond. and are promising sodium-ion battery cathode materials.  Manganese-based compds. have a high working potential vs. Na+/Na, and high capacity.  Yet, the layered nature of these materials means that they are prone to structural rearrangements at high voltage/low Na contents, the phase transformations and Na+ ion/vacancy ordering transitions resulting in capacity fade and poor reversibility.  This review discusses the latest advances in the field and focuses mainly on recent work on NayMn1-xMxO2 (x, y ≤ 1, M = Ni, Mg, Li) compds.  We compare the different lithium and sodium transition metal layered oxides (P2, O3, etc.) and describe the structures and mechanisms obsd. on alkali (de)intercalation.  The strategies used to enhance the electrochem. properties and stabilize the structural framework of sodium transition metal oxides are reviewed.  We show how X-ray diffraction and 7Li/23Na solid-state NMR can be combined to provide a detailed insight into the structural and electronic processes occurring upon electrochem. cycling of these materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp3iXys1AM5PLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljO1vZPF8mxKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslelu7rE&amp;md5=b77c52de27974cd2c817c5b39a68cd8a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1021/cm403855t"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, D.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Identifying the Critical Role of Li Substitution in P2-Nax[LiyNizMn1-y-z]O2 (0 &lt; x, y, z &lt; 1) Intercalation Cathode Materials for High-Energy Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Jing; Lee, Dae Hoe; Clement, Raphaele J.; Yu, Xiqian; Leskes, Michal; Pell, Andrew J.; Pintacuda, Guido; Yang, Xiao-Qing; Grey, Clare P.; Meng, Ying Shirley</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1260-1269</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Li-substituted layered P2-Na0.80[Li0.12Ni0.22Mn0.66]O2 is studied as an advanced cathode material for Na-ion batteries.  Both n diffraction and NMR spectroscopy are used to elucidate the local structure, and they reveal that most of the Li ions are located in transition metal (TM) sites, preferably surrounded by Mn ions.  To characterize structural changes occurring upon electrochem. cycling, in situ synchrotron x-ray diffraction is conducted.  No significant phase transformation is obsd. up to 4.4 V charge for this material, unlike Li-free P2-type Na cathodes.  The presence of monovalent Li ions in the TM layers allows more Na ions to reside in the prismatic sites, stabilizing the overall charge balance of the compd.  Consequently, more Na ions remain in the compd. upon charge, the P2 structure is retained in the high voltage region, and the phase transformation is delayed.  Ex situ NMR is conducted on samples at different states of charge/discharge to track Li-ion site occupation changes.  Surprisingly, Li is mobile, some Li ions migrate from the TM layer to the Na layer at high voltage, and yet this process is highly reversible.  Novel design principles for Na cathode materials are proposed from an atomistic level understanding of the underlying electrochem. processes.  These principles enable one to devise an optimized, high capacity, and structurally stable compd. as a potential cathode material for high-energy Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRaU2CEikYCrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljO1vZPF8mxKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVSluw%253D%253D&amp;md5=aebb4423baa75fe925ec0b0c2f7c0955</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.12.083"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhong, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">McDonald, M.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">P2-type Na0.66Ni0.33-xZnxMn0.67O2 as new high-voltage cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xuehang; Guo, Jianghuai; Wang, Dawei; Zhong, Guiming; McDonald, Matthew J.; Yang, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">281</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18-26</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-type Na0.66Ni0.33-xZnxMn0.67O2 (x = 0, 0.07, 0.14) are prepd. using a conventional solid state method and for the first time developed as promising cathode materials for high-voltage sodium-ion batteries.  The x-ray diffraction patterns show that Zn2+ ions are successfully incorporated into the lattice of the Na-Ni-Mn-O system and the P2-type structure remains unchanged after substitution.  The introduction of Zn2+ in the Na-Ni-Mn-O system can effectively overcome the drawback of voltage decay when charged to a higher cutoff voltage (&gt;4.0 V), and significantly improve capacity retention compared to the unsubstituted material during cycling.  In addn., a smoother charge/discharge profile can be obsd. between 3.0 and 4.0 V for Zn-substituted samples, demonstrating that Na+/vacancy ordering can be suppressed during sodium insertion/extn.  Na0.66Ni0.26Zn0.07Mn0.67O2 can deliver an initial capacity of 132 mA-h/g at 12 mA/g with a high av. voltage of 3.6 V and a capacity retention of 89% after 30 cycles.  Electrochem. impedance spectroscopy measurements demonstrate that Zn substitution is an effective way to limit the increase of inter-particle contact resistance by suppressing any possible irreversible phase transformation found at low sodium contents.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrmbpOEPj4Ld7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljO1vZPF8mxKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitFOqs7fN&amp;md5=0a2dab09a85de3fe2f0bd70e6b9ec3a0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b06701"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, G.-L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhong, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gong, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">McDonald, M.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insights into the Effects of Zinc Doping on Structural Phase Transition of P2-Type Sodium Nickel Manganese Oxide Cathodes for High-Energy Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xuehang; Xu, Gui-Liang; Zhong, Guiming; Gong, Zhengliang; McDonald, Matthew J.; Zheng, Shiyao; Fu, Riqiang; Chen, Zonghai; Amine, Khalil; Yang, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">22227-22237</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-type sodium nickel manganese oxide-based cathode materials with higher energy densities are prime candidates for applications in rechargeable sodium ion batteries.  A systematic study combining in situ high energy X-ray diffraction (HEXRD), ex situ X-ray absorption fine spectroscopy (XAFS), transmission electron microscopy (TEM), and solid-state NMR (SS-NMR) techniques was carried out to gain a deep insight into the structural evolution of P2-Na0.66Ni0.33-xZnxMn0.67O2 (x = 0, 0.07) during cycling.  In situ HEXRD and ex situ TEM measurements indicate that an irreversible phase transition occurs upon sodium insertion-extn. of Na0.66Ni0.33Mn0.67O2.  Zinc doping of this system results in a high structural reversibility.  XAFS measurements indicate that both materials are almost completely dependent on the Ni4+/Ni3+/Ni2+ redox couple to provide charge/discharge capacity.  SS-NMR measurements indicate that both reversible and irreversible migration of transition metal ions into the sodium layer occurs in the material at the fully charged state.  The irreversible migration of transition metal ions triggers a structural distortion, leading to the obsd. capacity and voltage fading.  Our results allow a new understanding of the importance of improving the stability of transition metal layers.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqyUPPhcNq0kLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljO1vZPF8mxKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht12jsbvM&amp;md5=f3a446894cd9f89f799beef61f2b49ee</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201602202"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, P.-F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">You, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yin, Y.-X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.-S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wan, L.-J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Y.-G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Suppressing the P2–O2 Phase Transition of Na<sub>0.67</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>Ni<sub>0.33</sub>O<sub>2</sub> by Magnesium Substitution for Improved Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A review of atomic layer deposition providing high performance lithium sulfur batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Bo; Li, Xifei; Bai, Zhimin; Song, Xiaosheng; Xiong, Dongbin; Zhao, Mengli; Li, Dejun; Lu, Shigang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the significant obstacles that have been conquered in lithium-sulfur (Li-S) batteries, it is urgent to impel accelerating development of room-temp. Li-S batteries with high energy d. and long-term stability.  In view of the unique solid-liq.-solid conversion processes of Li-S batteries, however, designing effective strategies to address the insulativity and vol. effect of cathode, shuttle of sol. polysulfides, and/or safety hazard of Li metal anode has been challenging.  An at. layer deposition (ALD) is a representative thin film technol. with exceptional capabilities in developing at.-precisely conformal films.  It has been demonstrated to be a promise strategy of solving emerging issues in advanced elec. energy storage (EES) devices via the surface modification and/or the fabrication of complex nanostructured materials.  In this review, the recent developments and significances on how ALD improves the performance of Li-S batteries were discussed in detail.  Significant attention mainly focused on the various strategies with the use of ALD to refine the electrochem. interfaces and cell configurations.  Furthermore, the novel opportunities and perspective assocd. with ALD for future research directions were summarized.  This review may boost the development and application of advanced Li-S batteries using ALD.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoFaf2EZ0-I0LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgh72aDUHg3fA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhvVChsbrE&amp;md5=2e726f3d48f62787ee3a3adbb828705d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1021/cr900056b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">George, S.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">ALD TiO2 coated silicon nanowires for lithium ion battery anodes with enhanced cycling stability and coulombic efficiency</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Memarzadeh Lotfabad, Elmira; Kalisvaart, Peter; Cui, Kai; Kohandehghan, Alireza; Kupsta, Martin; Olsen, Brian; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">32</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13646-13657</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PPCPFQ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1463-9076</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We demonstrate that silicon nanowire Li-ion battery anodes that are conformally coated with TiO2 using at. layer deposition (ALD) show a remarkable performance improvement.  The coulombic efficiency is increased to ∼99%, among the highest ever reported for silicon nanowires, as compared to 95% for the baseline uncoated samples.  The capacity retention after 100 cycles for the nanocomposite is twice as high as that of the baseline at 0.1C (60% vs. 30%), and more than three times higher at 5C (34% vs. 10%).  We also demonstrate that the microstructure of the coatings is critically important for achieving this effect.  Titanium dioxide coatings with an as-deposited anatase structure are nowhere near as effective as amorphous ones, the latter proving much more resistant to delamination from the silicon nanowire core.  We use TEM to demonstrate that upon lithiation the amorphous coating develops a highly dispersed nanostructure comprised of cryst. LiTiO2 and a secondary amorphous phase.  Electron energy loss spectroscopy combined with bulk and surface anal. techniques are employed to highlight the passivating effect of TiO2, which results in significantly fewer cycling-induced electrolyte decompn. products as compared to the bare nanowires.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpC8kF3vsCy8bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgh72aDUHg3fA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFOgtrbK&amp;md5=3e4312fca71381ff3178f9ac491fa1a8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1149/1.3258274"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jung, Y.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced Stability of LiCoO2 Cathodes in Lithium-Ion Batteries Using Surface Modification by Atomic Layer Deposition</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jung, Yoon Seok; Cavanagh, Andrew S.; Dillon, Anne C.; Groner, Markus D.; George, Steven M.; Lee, Se-Hee</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">157</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">A75-A81</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JESOAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultrathin at. layer deposition coatings enhance the performance of lithium-ion batteries.  Previous studies have demonstrated that LiCoO2 cathode powders coated with metal oxides with thicknesses of ∼100 to 1000 Å grown using wet chem. techniques improved lithium-ion battery performance.  In this study, LiCoO2 powders were coated with conformal Al2O3 at. layer deposition films with thicknesses of only ∼3 to 4 Å established using two at. layer deposition cycles.  The coated LiCoO2 powders exhibited a capacity retention of 89% after 120 charge-discharge cycles in the 3.3-4.5 V (vs. Li/Li+) range.  In contrast, the bare LiCoO2 powders displayed only a 45% capacity retention.  Al2O3 at. layer deposition films coated directly on the composite electrode also produced improved capacity retention.  This dramatic improvement may result from the ultrathin Al2O3 at. layer deposition film acting to minimize Co dissoln. or reduce surface electrolyte reactions.  Similar expts. with ultrathin ZnO at. layer deposition films did not display enhanced performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrgvujT0QkmTbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgh72aDUHg3fA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1MXhsFagur3O&amp;md5=2738e229c5cafacdf06e57050b93a087</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/jp210551r"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, H.-M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, F.-M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chu, J.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced Cycleability in Lithium Ion Batteries: Resulting from Atomic Layer Deposition of Al2O3 or TiO2 on LiCoO2 Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Ho-Ming; Wang, Fu-Ming; Chu, Jinn P.; Santhanam, Raman; Rick, John; Lo, Shen-Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">116</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7629-7637</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This study reports the prepn. of Al2O3 and TiO2 coatings on the as-prepd. LiCoO2 electrodes using at. layer deposition.  A thin Al2O3 at. layer deposition coating was shown to eliminate capacity fading effectively during repeated charging and discharging, whereas a TiO2 coating led to significant improvement only at high cycle nos.  An anal. of the differential capacity vs. potential curves suggests that this poorer cycling performance could be related to the participation of the TiO2 thin film in the redox reaction.  Graphical representation of the energy levels of the various at. layer deposition coatings on LiCoO2 during charging and discharging indicated that the redox current is impeded at the Al2O3-LiCoO2 junction, whereas electrons and holes were energetic enough to flow into the TiO2 because of the smaller band gap energy.  The barrier between the valence band maxima of TiO2 and LiCoO2 expands as the charge-discharge cycle no. increases, eventually making TiO2 redox-inactive.  These conclusions are supported by both XPS spectra and the cycle performance in the established literature refs.  Our results suggest that large band gap materials should be considered to be potentially useful at. layer deposition coatings on cathode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrJ1rShZf5YALVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgh72aDUHg3fA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xkt1Omt78%253D&amp;md5=53c395a4b705634739068a74f348d1a7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1007/s00339-010-6097-y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, J.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The effect of TiO2 coating on the electrochemical performance of ZnO nanorod as the anode material for lithium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Jian-Hong; Hon, Min-Hsiung; Chung, Yi-Wen; Leu, Ing-Chi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Physics A: Materials Science &amp; Processing</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">ZnO nanorods were coated with TiO2 thin film using the at. layer deposition process.  X-ray diffraction, SEM, and transmission electron microscopy were used to characterize the crystal structure and surface morphol. of the coated composites.  Results of galvanostatic charge and discharge tests and cyclic voltammetry suggest that lithium ions can reversibly intercalate into and deintercalate from TiO2-coated ZnO nanorods, and that stable cycling behavior in an ethylene carbonate-based electrolyte can be achieved.  The TiO2 coating is believed to reduce the degree of reaction electrodes have with the electrolyte during the charge-discharge process since the inactive coating layer prevents the electrode from having direct contact with the electrolyte.  Furthermore, the one-dimensional nanorods provide a relatively higher surface area than those of their bulk form or thin film, which allows a much greater portion of atoms on the surface to undergo the electrochem. reaction.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrathin atomic layer deposited ZrO2 coating to enhance the electrochemical performance of Li4Ti5O12 as an anode material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Jian; Li, Xifei; Cai, Mei; Li, Ruying; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">93</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">195-201</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Atomic layer deposition was used to deposit ZrO2 directly on Li4Ti5O12 electrode to improve its electrochem. performance.  The thickness of the deposited ZrO2 was controlled by adjusting at. layer deposition cycles from 0 to 1, 2, 5, 10 and 50.  The Li4Ti5O12 electrodes with and without ZrO2 coating were characterized by SEM, energy dispersive x-ray spectroscopy, high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy, cyclic voltammetry and galvanostatic charge-discharge tests.  The cyclic voltammetry results indicated that ZrO2 coating with 2, 5 and 10 at. layer deposition cycles could effectively reduce the electrochem. polarization of the Li4Ti5O12 electrode.  Charge-discharge test revealed that the Li4Ti5O12 electrodes with 1-, 2- and 5-cycle ZrO2 coating exhibited higher specific capacity, better cycling performance and rate capability than the pristine Li4Ti5O12 in a voltage range of 0.1-2.5 V.  However, ZrO2 coating with more than 5 at. layer deposition cycles could lead to degraded performance of Li4Ti5O12.  Mechanism for the enhanced electrochem. performance of Li4Ti5O12 was explored by electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, and the reason was attributed to the suppressed formation of solid electrolyte interphase and the improved electron transport by ultrathin ZrO2 coating.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqYJtEc1f55O7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lghYBDQ-yL07Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXjvFegsLY%253D&amp;md5=4f3e7e1997a6aec3f1aa9fbbfe1ffa88</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2005.11.015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, H.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cathode materials modified by surface coating for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, C.; Zhang, H. P.; Fu, L. J.; Liu, H.; Wu, Y. P.; Rahm, E.; Holze, R.; Wu, H. Q.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2006</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">51</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3872-3883</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Recent research results confirm the importance of structural surface features of cathode materials for their electrochem. performance.  Modification by coating is an important method to achieve improved electrochem. performance, and the latest progress is summarized.  When the surface of cathode materials including LiCoO2, LiNiO2, LiMn2O4 and LiMnO2 is coated with oxides such as MgO, Al2O3, SiO2, TiO2, ZnO, SnO2, ZrO2, Li2O·2B2O3-glass and other materials, the coatings prevent the direct contact with the electrolyte soln., suppress phase transition, improve the structural stability, and decrease the disorder of cations in crystal sites.  As a result, side reactions and heat generation during cycling are decreased.  Accompanying actions, such as suppression of Mn2+ dissoln., increase in cond. and removal of HF from electrolyte solns., have been obsd.  Consequently, marked improvement of electrochem. performance of electrode materials including reversible capacity, Coulomb efficiency in the first cycle, cycling behavior, rate capability and overcharge tolerance has been achieved.  Further directions are suggested for the surface modification of electrode materials.  With further understanding of the effects of the surface structure of cathode materials on lithium intercalation and de-intercalation, better and/or cheaper cathode materials from surface modification will come up in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpsZVjB0yoj1bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lghYBDQ-yL07Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD28XktleisLc%253D&amp;md5=6489647bf7fcfc3bcdc4dd3638cab5f7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1039/C3EE42704H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Banis, M.                 10.1039/C3EE42704H</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D7%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D768-778%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BLiu%26author%3DM.%2BN.%2BBanis%26author%3DA.%2BLushington%26author%3DR.%2BLi%26author%3DM.%2BCai%26author%3DX.%2BSun%26title%3DAtomic%2BLayer%2BDeposition%2Bof%2BSolid-State%2BElectrolyte%2BCoated%2BCathode%2BMaterials%2Bwith%2BSuperior%2BHigh-Voltage%2BCycling%2BBehavior%2Bfor%2BLithium%2BIon%2BBattery%2BApplication%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC3EE42704H&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b05326&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC3EE42704H&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomic layer deposition of solid-state electrolyte coated cathode materials with superior high-voltage cycling behavior for lithium ion battery application</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xifei; Liu, Jian; Banis, Mohammad Norouzi; Lushington, Andrew; Li, Ruying; Cai, Mei; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">768-778</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">LiNi1/3Co1/3Mn1/3O2 (NMC) is a highly promising cathode material for use in lithium ion batteries; unfortunately, its poor cycling performance at high cutoff voltages hinders its commercialization.  In this study, for the first time, we employ at. layer deposition (ALD) to coat lithium tantalum oxide, a solid-state electrolyte, with varying thicknesses on NMC in an attempt to improve battery performance.  Our results indicate that utilization of a solid-state electrolyte as a coating material for NMC significantly improves performance at high cutoff voltages but is strongly dependent on coating thicknesses.  Our investigation revealed that a thicker coating proved to be beneficial in preventing cathode material dissoln. into the electrolyte and aided in maintaining the microstructure of NMC.  Consequently, a thicker ALD coating resulted in increased electrochem. impedance of the cathode.  The results of this study indicate that an optimized coating thickness is needed in order to strike a balance between maintaining structural stability while minimizing electrochem. impedance.  The coating thicknesses are functionally specific, and for the best improvement of a cathode, a particular coating thickness should be sought.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr432_eespCI7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lghYBDQ-yL07Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhsFaksLc%253D&amp;md5=a4fb112025ec7d2324d0a78011c39ae9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.08.042"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Meng, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Banis, M.                 10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.08.042</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D247%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D57-69%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BLiu%26author%3DX.%2BMeng%26author%3DY.%2BTang%26author%3DM.%2BN.%2BBanis%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BHu%26author%3DR.%2BLi%26author%3DM.%2BCai%26author%3DX.%2BSun%26title%3DSignificant%2BImpact%2Bon%2BCathode%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BLithium-Ion%2BBatteries%2Bby%2BPrecisely%2BControlled%2BMetal%2BOxide%2BNanocoatings%2Bvia%2BAtomic%2BLayer%2BDeposition%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2013.08.042&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b05326&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2013.08.042&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Significant impact on cathode performance of lithium-ion batteries by precisely controlled metal oxide nanocoatings via atomic layer deposition</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xifei; Liu, Jian; Meng, Xiangbo; Tang, Yongji; Banis, Mohammad Norouzi; Yang, Jinli; Hu, Yuhai; Li, Ruying; Cai, Mei; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">247</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">57-69</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">LiCoO2 in the com. lithium ion batteries has been suffering from its poor cycling performance at high cutoff voltages.  In this study, the authors employ an at. layer deposition (ALD) technique to surface-modify a LiCoO2 material with various thickness-controlled metal oxide (TiO2, ZrO2 and Al2O3) coatings to improve its battery performance.  The effects of the metal oxide coatings on the electrochem. performance of LiCoO2 electrode are studied in detail.  It is demonstrated that a uniform and dense coating via the ALD route on LiCoO2 powder can lower the battery performance due to an obvious decrease in lithium diffusion and electron transport with the coating layers.  In contrast, it is revealed that a direct coating on prefabricated LiCoO2 electrodes performs much better than a coating on LiCoO2 powders.  It is further disclosed that the improved electrochem. performance of coated LiCoO2 electrode is highly dependent on the coating materials.  Of the three coating materials, the Al2O3 coating results in the best cycling stability while the ZrO2 coating contributes to the best rate capability.  It is thus suggested that the coating materials are functionally specific, and for the best improvement of a cathode, a particular coating material should be sought.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpQqKKnGMru9LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-eGBp6ohmvQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhs12lsbjN&amp;md5=dd244c78955b2b23a363be3adf54e652</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201200166"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Y.-S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Armand, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Disodium Terephthalate (Na<sub>2</sub>C<sub>8</sub>H<sub>4</sub>O<sub>4</sub>) as High Performance Anode Material for Low-Cost Room-Temperature Sodium-Ion Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Disodium terephthalate (Na2C8H4O4) as high performance anode material for low-cost room-temperature sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Liang; Zhao, Junmei; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Zhou, Zhibin; Armand, Michel; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The carboxylate-based org. material, disodium terephthalate (Na2C8H4O4) is firstly introduced as a novel anode material for low-cost rechargeable room-temp. Na-ion batteries.  The material exhibits low Na insertion voltage at 0.29 V.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered P2-Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 as high-voltage cathode for sodium-ion batteries: The capacity decay mechanism and Al2O3 surface modification</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yihang; Fang, Xin; Zhang, Anyi; Shen, Chenfei; Liu, Qingzhou; Enaya, Hani A.; Zhou, Chongwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The P2 type Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 is a high-voltage cathode material for Na-ion batteries with a theor. capacity of 173 mA h/g and a long operation voltage plateau of 4.2 V.  However, the material has exhibited unstable cycling performance within the high-voltage window, which severely limits its application.  Moreover, its capacity decay mechanism is still unclear.  In this study, we first investigate the difference between as-prepd. and after-cycling Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 samples, and then confirmed that the transition metal oxide layer exfoliation assocd. with the crystal phase transition during Na ion extn. and insertion is the main cause of capacity fading.  The Al2O3 coated Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 with enhanced cycling performance was prepd. by taking the benefit of Al2O3 coating.  The Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 sample without any surface modification presented a 164 mA h/g initial specific discharge capacity within the voltage window from 2.5 V to 4.3 V, and the capacity decayed to 44 mA h/g at the 300th cycle, resulting in only a 26.8% retention.  In contrast, the Al2O3-coated Na2/3[Ni1/3Mn2/3]O2 presented a similar initial capacity, but with an enhanced 73.2% retention after 300 cycles.  The enhanced cycling stability obsd. in after-cycling characterization and anal. confirms that the Al2O3 surface coating can effectively suppress the unfavorable side reaction at high voltage and the exfoliation of the metal oxide layers.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqwO8gmvj_Iv7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-eGBp6ohmvQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtFCrsbzM&amp;md5=65d57c83995b13acf248dff048736de2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b02158"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sina, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Parikh, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Uekert, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shahbazian, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Devaraj, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Meng, Y.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Role of 4-tert-Butylpyridine as a Hole Transport Layer Morphological Controller in Perovskite Solar Cells</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Shen; Sina, Mahsa; Parikh, Pritesh; Uekert, Taylor; Shahbazian, Brian; Devaraj, Arun; Meng, Ying Shirley</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid org.-inorg. materials for high-efficiency, low-cost photovoltaic devices have seen rapid progress since the introduction of lead based perovskites and solid-state hole transport layers.  Although majority of the materials used for perovskite solar cells (PSC) are introduced from dye-sensitized solar cells (DSSCs), the presence of a perovskite capping layer as opposed to a single dye mol. (in DSSCs) changes the interactions between the various layers in perovskite solar cells. 4-tert-Butylpyridine (tBP), commonly used in PSCs, is assumed to function as a charge recombination inhibitor, similar to DSSCs.  However, the presence of a perovskite capping layer calls for a re-evaluation of its function in PSCs.  Using TEM (transmission electron microscopy), we first confirm the role of tBP as a HTL morphol. controller in PSCs.  Our observations suggest that tBP significantly improves the uniformity of the HTL and avoids accumulation of Li salt.  We also study degrdn. pathways by using FTIR (Fourier transform IR spectroscopy) and APT (atom probe tomog.) to investigate and visualize in 3-dimensions the moisture content assocd. with the Li salt.  Long-term effects, over 1000 h, due to evapn. of tBP have also been studied.  Based on our findings, a PSC failure mechanism assocd. with the morphol. change of the HTL is proposed. tBP, the morphol. controller in HTL, plays a key role in this process, and thus this study highlights the need for additive materials with higher b.ps. for consistent long-term performance of PSCs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpKVK_Iqh022bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-eGBp6ohmvQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtlOqu7vO&amp;md5=2ecb5f8cb1dc4bea8bc1871415bbd58f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.ultramic.2010.11.027"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, M.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Minimization of focused ion beam damage in nanostructured polymer thin films</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Suhan; Park, Moon Jeong; Balsara, Nitash P.; Liu, Gao; Minor, Andrew M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Ultramicroscopy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Focused ion beam (FIB) instruments have proven to be an invaluable tool for transmission electron microscopy (TEM) sample prepn.  FIBs enable relatively easy and site-specific cross-sectioning of different classes of materials.  However, damage mechanisms due to ion bombardment and possible beam heating effects in materials limit the usefulness of FIBs.  Materials with adequate heat cond. do not suffer from beam heating during FIB prepn., and artifacts in materials such as metals and ceramics are primarily limited to defect generation and Ga implantation.  However, in materials such as polymers or biol. structures, where heat cond. is low, beam heating can also be a problem.  In order to examine FIB damage in polymers we have undertaken a systematic study by exposing sections of a PS-b-PMMA block copolymer to the ion beam at varying beam currents and sample temps.  The sections were then examd. by TEM and SEM and analyzed using electron energy loss spectroscopy (EELS).  Our empirical results show beam heating in polymers due to FIB prepn. can be limited by maintaining a low beam current (≤100 pA) during milling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoyrV1CjnoIMrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li-eGBp6ohmvQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXitFWqtbo%253D&amp;md5=4e385c1960825439e67d64b76c09f784</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2013.03.010"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Malmgren, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ciosek, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hahlin, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gustafsson, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gorgoi, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rensmo, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Edström, K.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Comparing Anode and Cathode Electrode/electrolyte Interface Composition and Morphology Using Soft and Hard X-Ray Photoelectron Spectroscopy</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of Surface Modification on Nano-Structured LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 Spinel Materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cho, Hyung-Man; Chen, Michael Vincent; MacRae, Alex C.; Meng, Ying Shirley</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">30</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fine-tuning of particle size and morphol. has been shown to result in differential material performance in the area of secondary lithium-ion batteries.  For instance, redn. of particle size to the nanoregime typically leads to better transport of electrochem. active species by increasing the amt. of reaction sites as a result of higher electrode surface area.  The spinel-phase oxide LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 (LNMO), was prepd. using a sol-gel based template synthesis to yield nanowire morphol. without any addnl. binders or electronic conducting agents.  Therefore, proper experimentation of the nanosize effect can be achieved in this study.  The spinel phase LMNO is a high energy electrode material currently being explored for use in lithium-ion batteries, with a specific capacity of 146 mAh/g and high-voltage plateau at ∼4.7 V (vs. Li/Li+).  However, research has shown that extensive electrolyte decompn. and the formation of a surface passivation layer results when LMNO is implemented as a cathode in electrochem. cells.  As a result of the high surface area assocd. with nanosized particles, manganese ion dissoln. results in capacity fading over prolonged cycling.  In order to prevent these detrimental effects without compromising electrochem. performance, various coating methods were explored.  In this work, TiO2 and Al2O3 thin films were deposited using at. layer deposition (ALD) on the surface of LNMO particles.  This resulted in effective surface protection by prevention of electrolyte side reactions and a sharp redn. in resistance at the electrode/electrolyte interface region.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpTcKqThsV5erVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhW0FRDXUgOcA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFOmsrfN&amp;md5=d18bb790c669b2e3bd8d50ddaca53db4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.10.207"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, J.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Surface chemistry of LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 particles coated by Al2O3 using atomic layer deposition for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Jin Wook; Kim, Dong Hyeon; Oh, Dae Yang; Lee, Hyeyoun; Kim, Ji Hyun; Lee, Jae Hyun; Jung, Yoon Seok</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
